Crusade">Third Crusade</a> (1189&#8211;1192)</div></div></div>\n<p>The Middle Ages on the mainland were dominated by the two upper echelons of the social structure: the nobility and the clergy. <a href="/wiki/Feudalism" title="Feudalism">Feudalism</a> developed in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> in the Early Middle Ages and soon spread throughout Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_158_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_158-76">[76]</a></sup> A struggle for influence between the <a href="/wiki/Nobility" title="Nobility">nobility</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy" title="Monarchy">monarchy</a> in England led to the writing of the <a href="/wiki/Magna_Carta" title="Magna Carta">Magna Carta</a> and the establishment of a <a href="/wiki/Parliament" title="Parliament">parliament</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_186_77-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_186-77">[77]</a></sup> The primary source of culture in this period came from the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>. Through monasteries and cathedral schools, the Church was responsible for education in much of Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_158_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_158-76">[76]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Papacy" title="Papacy">Papacy</a> reached the height of its power during the High Middle Ages. An <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East-West_Schism" title="East-West Schism">East-West Schism</a> in 1054 split the former Roman Empire religiously, with the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Orthodox_Church" title="Eastern Orthodox Church">Eastern Orthodox Church</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantine Empire</a> and the Roman Catholic Church in the former Western Roman Empire. In 1095 <a href="/wiki/Pope_Urban_II" title="Pope Urban II">Pope Urban II</a> called for a <a href="/wiki/Crusades" title="Crusades">crusade</a> against <a href="/wiki/Muslims" title="Muslims">Muslims</a> occupying <a href="/wiki/Jerusalem" title="Jerusalem">Jerusalem</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Holy_Land" title="Holy Land">Holy Land</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_192_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_192-78">[78]</a></sup> In Europe itself, the Church organised the <a href="/wiki/Inquisition" title="Inquisition">Inquisition</a> against heretics. In <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Reconquista" title="Reconquista">Reconquista</a> concluded with the fall of <a href="/wiki/Granada" title="Granada">Granada</a> in 1492, ending over seven centuries of Islamic rule in the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_199_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_199-79">[79]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In the east a resurgent Byzantine Empire recaptured Crete and Cyprus from the Muslims and reconquered the Balkans. Constantinople was the largest and wealthiest city in Europe from the 9th to the 12th centuries, with a population of approximately 400,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> The Empire was weakened following the defeat at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Manzikert" title="Battle of Manzikert">Manzikert</a> and was weakened considerably by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Constantinople_(1204)" title="Siege of Constantinople (1204)">sack of Constantinople in 1204</a>, during the <a href="/wiki/Fourth_Crusade" title="Fourth Crusade">Fourth Crusade</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DuikerSpielvogel2010_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-DuikerSpielvogel2010-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Findlay2006_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Findlay2006-82">[82]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Browning1992_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-Browning1992-83">[83]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Byfield2008_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-Byfield2008-84">[84]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Golna2004_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-Golna2004-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Powell2001_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-Powell2001-86">[86]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Irvin2002_87-0"><a href="#cite_note-Irvin2002-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Frucht2004_88-0"><a href="#cite_note-Frucht2004-88">[88]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-DuikerSpielvogel2010v2_89-0"><a href="#cite_note-DuikerSpielvogel2010v2-89">[89]</a></sup> Although it would recover Constantinople in 1261, <a href="/wiki/Byzantine_Empire" title="Byzantine Empire">Byzantium</a> <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">fell in 1453</a> when <a href="/wiki/Fall_of_Constantinople" title="Fall of Constantinople">Constantinople was taken</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_211_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_211-90">[90]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Peters2006_91-0"><a href="#cite_note-Peters2006-91">[91]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chronicles_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chronicles-92">[92]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mongols_suzdal.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1282" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="272" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Mongols_suzdal.jpg/170px-Mongols_suzdal.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Mongols_suzdal.jpg/255px-Mongols_suzdal.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/56/Mongols_suzdal.jpg/340px-Mongols_suzdal.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mongols_suzdal.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The sacking of <a href="/wiki/Suzdal" title="Suzdal">Suzdal</a> by <a href="/wiki/Batu_Khan" title="Batu Khan">Batu Khan</a> in 1238, during the <a href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Europe" title="Mongol invasion of Europe">Mongol invasion of Europe</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the 11th and 12th centuries, constant incursions by nomadic <a href="/wiki/Turkic_peoples" title="Turkic peoples">Turkic</a> tribes, such as the <a href="/wiki/Pechenegs" title="Pechenegs">Pechenegs</a> and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuman-Kipchak_Confederation" title="Cuman-Kipchak Confederation">Cuman-Kipchaks</a>, caused a massive migration of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slavic_peoples" title="Slavic peoples">Slavic</a> populations to the safer, heavily forested regions of the north and temporarily halted the expansion of the Rus\' state to the south and east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Klyuch1_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-Klyuch1-93">[93]</a></sup> Like many other parts of <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasia</a>, these territories were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mongol_invasion_of_Rus" title="Mongol invasion of Rus">overrun by the Mongols</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup> The invaders, who became known as <a href="/wiki/Tatars" title="Tatars">Tatars</a>, were mostly Turkic-speaking peoples under Mongol suzerainty. They established the state of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a> with headquarters in Crimea, which later adopted Islam as a religion and ruled over modern-day southern and central Russia for more than three centuries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> After the collapse of Mongol dominions, the first Romanian states (principalities) emerged in the 14th century: Moldova and Walachia. Previously, these territories were under the successive control of Pechenegs and Cumans.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> From the 12th to the 15th centuries, the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Moscow" title="Grand Duchy of Moscow">Grand Duchy of Moscow</a> grew from a small principality under Mongol rule to the largest state in Europe, overthrowing the Mongols in 1480 and eventually becoming the <a href="/wiki/Tsardom_of_Russia" title="Tsardom of Russia">Tsardom of Russia</a>. The state was consolidated under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ivan_III_the_Great" title="Ivan III the Great">Ivan III the Great</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ivan_the_Terrible" title="Ivan the Terrible">Ivan the Terrible</a>, steadily expanding to the east and south over the next centuries.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Great_Famine_of_1315%E2%80%931317" title="Great Famine of 1315&#8211;1317">Great Famine of 1315&#8211;1317</a> was the first <a href="/wiki/Crisis_of_the_Late_Middle_Ages" title="Crisis of the Late Middle Ages">crisis</a> that would strike Europe in the late Middle Ages.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup> The period between 1348 and 1420 witnessed the heaviest loss. The population of <a href="/wiki/France_in_the_Middle_Ages" title="France in the Middle Ages">France</a> was reduced by half.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-100"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> Medieval Britain was afflicted by 95 famines,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101">[101]</a></sup> and France suffered the effects of 75 or more in the same period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102">[102]</a></sup> Europe was devastated in the mid-14th century by the <a href="/wiki/Black_Death" title="Black Death">Black Death</a>, one of the most deadly <a href="/wiki/Pandemic" title="Pandemic">pandemics</a> in human history which killed an estimated 25&#160;million people in Europe alone&#8212;a third of the <a href="/wiki/Medieval_demography" title="Medieval demography">European population</a> at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The plague had a devastating effect on Europe\'s social structure; it induced people to live for the moment as illustrated by <a href="/wiki/Giovanni_Boccaccio" title="Giovanni Boccaccio">Giovanni Boccaccio</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Decameron" title="The Decameron">The Decameron</a></i> (1353). It was a serious blow to the Roman Catholic Church and led to increased <a href="/wiki/Persecution_of_Jews" title="Persecution of Jews">persecution of Jews</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beggars" title="Beggars">beggars</a>, and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leper" title="Leper">lepers</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_223_104-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_223-104">[104]</a></sup> The plague is thought to have returned every generation with varying <a href="/wiki/Virulence" title="Virulence">virulence</a> and mortalities until the 18th century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup> During this period, more than 100 plague <a href="/wiki/List_of_epidemics" title="List of epidemics">epidemics</a> swept across Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Revill_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-Revill-106">[106]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_modern_period">Early modern period</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Early_modern_period" title="Early modern period">Early modern period</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Renaissance" title="Renaissance">Renaissance</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Scientific_Revolution" title="Scientific Revolution">Scientific Revolution</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Discovery" title="Age of Discovery">Age of Discovery</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:La_scuola_di_Atene.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2277" data-file-width="3196" decoding="async" height="185" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/La_scuola_di_Atene.jpg/260px-La_scuola_di_Atene.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/La_scuola_di_Atene.jpg/390px-La_scuola_di_Atene.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/La_scuola_di_Atene.jpg/520px-La_scuola_di_Atene.jpg 2x" width="260"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:La_scuola_di_Atene.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/School_of_Athens" title="School of Athens"><i>The School of Athens</i></a> by <a href="/wiki/Raphael" title="Raphael">Raphael</a> (1511): Contemporaries such as <a href="/wiki/Michelangelo" title="Michelangelo">Michelangelo</a> and <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a> (centre) are portrayed as classical scholars.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Montsoreau(Maine-et-Loire).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Montsoreau%28Maine-et-Loire%29.jpg/220px-Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Montsoreau%28Maine-et-Loire%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Montsoreau%28Maine-et-Loire%29.jpg/330px-Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Montsoreau%28Maine-et-Loire%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Montsoreau%28Maine-et-Loire%29.jpg/440px-Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Montsoreau%28Maine-et-Loire%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Montsoreau(Maine-et-Loire).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The end of the <a href="/wiki/Hundred_Years%27_War" title="Hundred Years\' War">Hundred Years\' War</a> marked the beginning of the <a href="/wiki/French_Renaissance" title="French Renaissance">French Renaissance</a> in <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ch%C3%A2teau_de_Montsoreau" title="Ch&#226;teau de Montsoreau">Ch&#226;teau de Montsoreau</a> (1453).</div></div></div>\n<p>The Renaissance was a period of cultural change originating in <a href="/wiki/Florence" title="Florence">Florence</a> and later spreading to the rest of Europe. The rise of a <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_humanism" title="Renaissance humanism">new humanism</a> was accompanied by the recovery of forgotten <a href="/wiki/Classical_Greece" title="Classical Greece">classical Greek</a> and Arabic knowledge from <a href="/wiki/Monasticism" title="Monasticism">monastic</a> libraries, often translated from Arabic into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barrett_107-0"><a href="#cite_note-Barrett-107">[107]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108">[108]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The Renaissance spread across Europe between the 14th and 16th centuries: it saw the flowering of <a href="/wiki/Renaissance_art" title="Renaissance art">art</a>, <a href="/wiki/Philosophy" title="Philosophy">philosophy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Music" title="Music">music</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/History_of_science_in_the_Renaissance" title="History of science in the Renaissance">sciences</a>, under the joint patronage of <a href="/wiki/Royal_family" title="Royal family">royalty</a>, the nobility, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a>, and an emerging merchant class.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_254_110-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_254-110">[110]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup> Patrons in Italy, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Medici" title="Medici">Medici</a> family of Florentine bankers and the <a href="/wiki/Pope" title="Pope">Popes</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rome" title="Rome">Rome</a>, funded prolific <a href="/wiki/Quattrocento" title="Quattrocento">quattrocento</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cinquecento" title="Cinquecento">cinquecento</a> artists such as <a href="/wiki/Raphael" title="Raphael">Raphael</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michelangelo" title="Michelangelo">Michelangelo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_da_Vinci" title="Leonardo da Vinci">Leonardo da Vinci</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_292_113-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_292-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Political intrigue within the Church in the mid-14th century caused the <a href="/wiki/Western_Schism" title="Western Schism">Western Schism</a>. During this forty-year period, two popes&#8212;one in <a href="/wiki/Avignon" title="Avignon">Avignon</a> and one in Rome&#8212;claimed rulership over the Church. Although the schism was eventually healed in 1417, the papacy\'s spiritual authority had suffered greatly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_193_115-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_193-115">[115]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Lucas_Cranach_d.%C3%84._-_Martin_Luther,_1528_(Veste_Coburg).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3400" data-file-width="2148" decoding="async" height="269" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Lucas_Cranach_d.%C3%84._-_Martin_Luther%2C_1528_%28Veste_Coburg%29.jpg/170px-Lucas_Cranach_d.%C3%84._-_Martin_Luther%2C_1528_%28Veste_Coburg%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Lucas_Cranach_d.%C3%84._-_Martin_Luther%2C_1528_%28Veste_Coburg%29.jpg/255px-Lucas_Cranach_d.%C3%84._-_Martin_Luther%2C_1528_%28Veste_Coburg%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/90/Lucas_Cranach_d.%C3%84._-_Martin_Luther%2C_1528_%28Veste_Coburg%29.jpg/340px-Lucas_Cranach_d.%C3%84._-_Martin_Luther%2C_1528_%28Veste_Coburg%29.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Lucas_Cranach_d.%C3%84._-_Martin_Luther,_1528_(Veste_Coburg).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a> (1483&#8211;1546) initiated the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant_Reformation" title="Protestant Reformation">Protestant Reformation</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In the 15th century, Europe started to extend itself beyond its geographic frontiers. Spain and Portugal, the greatest naval powers of the time, took the lead in exploring the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-116"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_296_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_296-117">[117]</a></sup> Exploration reached the <a href="/wiki/Southern_Hemisphere" title="Southern Hemisphere">Southern Hemisphere</a> in the Atlantic and the Southern tip of Africa. <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Columbus" title="Christopher Columbus">Christopher Columbus</a> reached the <a href="/wiki/New_World" title="New World">New World</a> in 1492, and <a href="/wiki/Vasco_da_Gama" title="Vasco da Gama">Vasco da Gama</a> opened the ocean route to the <a href="/wiki/Orient" title="Orient">East</a> linking the Atlantic and <a href="/wiki/Indian_Ocean" title="Indian Ocean">Indian Oceans</a> in 1498. <a href="/wiki/Ferdinand_Magellan" title="Ferdinand Magellan">Ferdinand Magellan</a> reached Asia westward across the Atlantic and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Oceans</a> in the Spanish expedition of Magellan-Elcano, resulting in the first <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Timeline_of_Magellan%27s_circumnavigation" title="Timeline of Magellan\'s circumnavigation">circumnavigation of the globe</a>, completed by <a href="/wiki/Juan_Sebasti%C3%A1n_Elcano" title="Juan Sebasti&#225;n Elcano">Juan Sebasti&#225;n Elcano</a> (1519-1522). Soon after the Spanish and Portuguese began establishing large global empires in the Americas, Asia, Africa and Oceania.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_338_118-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_338-118">[118]</a></sup> France, the Netherlands and England soon followed in building large colonial empires with vast holdings in Africa, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Americas" title="The Americas">the Americas</a>, and Asia.\n</p><p>The Church\'s power was further weakened by the Protestant Reformation (1517&#8211;1648), initially sparked by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Ninety-Five_Theses" title="The Ninety-Five Theses">the works</a> of German theologian <a href="/wiki/Martin_Luther" title="Martin Luther">Martin Luther</a>, an attempt to start a reform within the Church. The Reformation also damaged the Holy Roman Emperor\'s influence, as German princes became divided between <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant">Protestant</a> and Roman Catholic faiths.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_256_119-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_256-119">[119]</a></sup> This eventually led to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thirty_Years_War" title="Thirty Years War">Thirty Years War</a> (1618&#8211;1648), which crippled the Holy Roman Empire and devastated much of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Modern_history_of_Germany" title="Early Modern history of Germany">Germany</a>, killing between 25 and 40 percent of its population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> In the aftermath of the <a href="/wiki/Peace_of_Westphalia" title="Peace of Westphalia">Peace of Westphalia</a>, France rose to predominance within Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_269_121-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_269-121">[121]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The 17th century in southern, central and eastern Europe was a period of general <a href="/wiki/The_General_Crisis" title="The General Crisis">decline</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup> Central and Eastern Europe experienced more than 150 famines in a 200-year period between 1501 and 1700.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup> From the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Krewo" title="Union of Krewo">Union of Krewo</a> (1385) central and eastern Europe was dominated by <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Poland_(1385%E2%80%931569)" title="Kingdom of Poland (1385&#8211;1569)">Kingdom of Poland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Grand_Duchy_of_Lithuania" title="Grand Duchy of Lithuania">Grand Duchy of Lithuania</a>. Between 1648 and 1655 in the central and eastern Europe ended hegemony of the <a href="/wiki/Polish%E2%80%93Lithuanian_Commonwealth" title="Polish&#8211;Lithuanian Commonwealth">Polish&#8211;Lithuanian Commonwealth</a>. From the 15th to 18th centuries, when the disintegrating khanates of the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Horde" title="Golden Horde">Golden Horde</a> were conquered by Russia, <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Tatars" title="Crimean Tatars">Tatars</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_Khanate" title="Crimean Khanate">Crimean Khanate</a> frequently <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crimean-Nogai_raids_into_East_Slavic_lands" title="Crimean-Nogai raids into East Slavic lands">raided</a> Eastern Slavic lands to capture slaves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-124"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> Further east, the <a href="/wiki/Nogai_Horde" title="Nogai Horde">Nogai Horde</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kazakh_Khanate" title="Kazakh Khanate">Kazakh Khanate</a> frequently raided the Slavic-speaking areas of Russia, Ukraine and Poland for hundreds of years, until the Russian expansion and conquest of most of northern Eurasia (i.e. Eastern Europe, Central Asia and Siberia). Meanwhile, in the south, the Ottomans had conquered the Balkans by the 15th century, <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Vienna" title="Siege of Vienna">laying siege to Vienna in 1529</a>. In the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lepanto" title="Battle of Lepanto">Battle of Lepanto</a> in 1571, the <a href="/wiki/Holy_League_(1571)" title="Holy League (1571)">Holy League</a> checked Ottoman power in the Mediterranean. The Ottomans again laid siege to Vienna in 1683, but the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Vienna" title="Battle of Vienna">Battle of Vienna</a> permanently ended their advance into Europe, and marked the political hegemony of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg_dynasty" title="Habsburg dynasty">Habsburg dynasty</a> in central Europe.\n</p><p>The Renaissance and the <a href="/wiki/New_Monarchs" title="New Monarchs">New Monarchs</a> marked the start of an Age of Discovery, a period of exploration, invention, and scientific development.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> Among the great figures of the Western <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scientific_revolution" title="Scientific revolution">scientific revolution</a> of the 16th and 17th centuries were <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Copernicus" title="Copernicus">Copernicus</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kepler" title="Kepler">Kepler</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Galileo" title="Galileo">Galileo</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Isaac_Newton" title="Isaac Newton">Isaac Newton</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> According to Peter Barrett, "It is widely accepted that \'modern science\' arose in the Europe of the 17th century (towards the end of the Renaissance), introducing a new understanding of the natural world."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Barrett_107-1"><a href="#cite_note-Barrett-107">[107]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="18th_and_19th_centuries">18th and 19th centuries</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Modern_history" title="Modern history">Modern history</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a>, <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Age_of_Enlightenment" title="Age of Enlightenment">Age of Enlightenment</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="570" data-file-width="800" decoding="async" height="157" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg/220px-Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg/330px-Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg/440px-Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Napoleons_retreat_from_moscow.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon</a>\'s retreat from Russia in 1812. Napoleon\'s <i><a href="/wiki/Grande_Arm%C3%A9e" title="Grande Arm&#233;e">Grande Arm&#233;e</a></i> had lost about half a million men.</div></div></div>\n<p>The Age of Enlightenment was a powerful intellectual movement during the 18th century promoting scientific and reason-based thoughts.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127">[127]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_255_129-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_255-129">[129]</a></sup> Discontent with the aristocracy and clergy\'s monopoly on political power in France resulted in the French Revolution and the establishment of the <a href="/wiki/French_First_Republic" title="French First Republic">First Republic</a> as a result of which the monarchy and many of the nobility perished during the initial <a href="/wiki/Reign_of_Terror" title="Reign of Terror">reign of terror</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Napoleon" title="Napoleon">Napoleon Bonaparte</a> rose to power in the aftermath of the French Revolution and established the <a href="/wiki/First_French_Empire" title="First French Empire">First French Empire</a> that, during the <a href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Wars" title="Napoleonic Wars">Napoleonic Wars</a>, grew to encompass large parts of Europe before collapsing in 1815 with the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Waterloo" title="Battle of Waterloo">Battle of Waterloo</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_360_131-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_360-131">[131]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-132"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleonic_Empire" title="Napoleonic Empire">Napoleonic rule</a> resulted in the further dissemination of the ideals of the French Revolution, including that of the <a href="/wiki/Nation_state" title="Nation state">nation-state</a>, as well as the widespread adoption of the French models of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Centralised_government" title="Centralised government">administration</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Napoleonic_code" title="Napoleonic code">law</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Education_in_France" title="Education in France">education</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_350_135-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_350-135">[135]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Vienna" title="Congress of Vienna">Congress of Vienna</a>, convened after Napoleon\'s downfall, established a new <a href="/wiki/Balance_of_power_(international_relations)" title="Balance of power (international relations)">balance of power</a> in Europe centred on the five "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Power" title="Great Power">Great Powers</a>": the UK, France, <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austrian_Empire" title="Austrian Empire">Austria</a>, and Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_367_136-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_367-136">[136]</a></sup> This balance would remain in place until the <a href="/wiki/Revolutions_of_1848" title="Revolutions of 1848">Revolutions of 1848</a>, during which liberal uprisings affected all of Europe except for Russia and the UK. These revolutions were eventually put down by conservative elements and few reforms resulted.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_371_137-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_371-137">[137]</a></sup> The year 1859 saw the unification of Romania, as a nation-state, from smaller principalities. In 1867, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Austro-Hungarian_empire" title="Austro-Hungarian empire">Austro-Hungarian empire</a> was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ausgleich" title="Ausgleich">formed</a>; and 1871 saw the unifications of both <a href="/wiki/Italian_unification" title="Italian unification">Italy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Unification_of_Germany" title="Unification of Germany">Germany</a> as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nation-states" title="Nation-states">nation-states</a> from smaller principalities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In parallel, the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Question" title="Eastern Question">Eastern Question</a> grew more complex ever since the Ottoman defeat in the <a href="/wiki/Russo-Turkish_War_(1768%E2%80%931774)" title="Russo-Turkish War (1768&#8211;1774)">Russo-Turkish War (1768&#8211;1774)</a>. As the dissolution of the Ottoman Empire seemed imminent, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_Power" title="Great Power">Great Powers</a> struggled to safeguard their strategic and commercial interests in the Ottoman domains. The <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russian Empire</a> stood to benefit from the decline, whereas the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habsburg_Empire" title="Habsburg Empire">Habsburg Empire</a> and <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Britain</a> perceived the preservation of the Ottoman Empire to be in their best interests. Meanwhile, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Serbian_revolution" title="Serbian revolution">Serbian revolution</a> (1804) and <a href="/wiki/Greek_War_of_Independence" title="Greek War of Independence">Greek War of Independence</a> (1821) marked the beginning of the end of Ottoman rule in the <a href="/wiki/Balkans" title="Balkans">Balkans</a>, which ended with the <a href="/wiki/Balkan_Wars" title="Balkan Wars">Balkan Wars</a> in 1912-1913.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup> Formal recognition of the <i>de facto</i> independent principalities of <a href="/wiki/Montenegro" title="Montenegro">Montenegro</a>, <a href="/wiki/Principality_of_Serbia" title="Principality of Serbia">Serbia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a> ensued at the <a href="/wiki/Congress_of_Berlin" title="Congress of Berlin">Congress of Berlin</a> in 1878.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marshall%27s_flax-mill,_Holbeck,_Leeds_-_interior_-_c.1800.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="957" data-file-width="1254" decoding="async" height="168" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Marshall%27s_flax-mill%2C_Holbeck%2C_Leeds_-_interior_-_c.1800.jpg/220px-Marshall%27s_flax-mill%2C_Holbeck%2C_Leeds_-_interior_-_c.1800.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Marshall%27s_flax-mill%2C_Holbeck%2C_Leeds_-_interior_-_c.1800.jpg/330px-Marshall%27s_flax-mill%2C_Holbeck%2C_Leeds_-_interior_-_c.1800.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Marshall%27s_flax-mill%2C_Holbeck%2C_Leeds_-_interior_-_c.1800.jpg/440px-Marshall%27s_flax-mill%2C_Holbeck%2C_Leeds_-_interior_-_c.1800.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marshall%27s_flax-mill,_Holbeck,_Leeds_-_interior_-_c.1800.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Marshall\'s <a href="/wiki/Temple_Works" title="Temple Works">Temple Works</a> (1840), the <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> started in <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a></div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Industrial_Revolution" title="Industrial Revolution">Industrial Revolution</a> started in <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Great_Britain" title="Kingdom of Great Britain">Great Britain</a> in the last part of the 18th century and spread throughout Europe. The invention and implementation of new technologies resulted in rapid urban growth, mass employment, and the rise of a new working class.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> Reforms in social and economic spheres followed, including the <a href="/wiki/Factory_Acts" title="Factory Acts">first laws</a> on <a href="/wiki/Child_labour" title="Child labour">child labour</a>, the legalisation of <a href="/wiki/Trade_union" title="Trade union">trade unions</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Abolitionism_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="Abolitionism in the United Kingdom">abolition of slavery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup> In Britain, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Public_Health_Act_of_1875" title="Public Health Act of 1875">Public Health Act of 1875</a> was passed, which significantly improved living conditions in many British cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup> Europe\'s population increased from about 100 million in 1700 to 400 million by 1900.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup> The last major famine recorded in Western Europe, the <a href="/wiki/Great_Famine_(Ireland)" title="Great Famine (Ireland)">Irish Potato Famine</a>, caused death and mass emigration of millions of Irish people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup> In the 19th century, 70&#160;million people left Europe in migrations to various European colonies abroad and to the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-146"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> Demographic growth meant that, by 1900, Europe\'s share of the world\'s population was 25%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="20th_century_to_the_present">20th century to the present</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Modern_era" title="Modern era">Modern era</a> and <a href="/wiki/History_of_Europe" title="History of Europe">History of Europe</a></div>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>, <a href="/wiki/Interwar_period" title="Interwar period">Interwar period</a>, <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cold_War" title="Cold War">Cold War</a>, and <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_European_Union" title="History of the European Union">History of the European Union</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Leaders_of_the_Central_Powers_-_Vierbund.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="340" data-file-width="525" decoding="async" height="142" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Leaders_of_the_Central_Powers_-_Vierbund.jpg/220px-Leaders_of_the_Central_Powers_-_Vierbund.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Leaders_of_the_Central_Powers_-_Vierbund.jpg/330px-Leaders_of_the_Central_Powers_-_Vierbund.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Leaders_of_the_Central_Powers_-_Vierbund.jpg/440px-Leaders_of_the_Central_Powers_-_Vierbund.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Leaders_of_the_Central_Powers_-_Vierbund.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Leaders of the Central Powers in 1918 (left to right): Kaiser <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wilhelm_II" title="Wilhelm II">Wilhelm II</a> of Germany, Kaiser <a href="/wiki/Franz_Joseph_I_of_Austria" title="Franz Joseph I of Austria">Franz Joseph</a> of Austria-Hungary, Sultan <a href="/wiki/Mehmed_V" title="Mehmed V">Mehmed V</a> of the Ottoman Empire, and Tsar <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ferdinand_of_Bulgaria" title="Ferdinand of Bulgaria">Ferdinand of Bulgaria</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Map_Europe_WW1_Frontlines_as_of_1916.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="593" data-file-width="1002" decoding="async" height="130" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Map_Europe_WW1_Frontlines_as_of_1916.png/220px-Map_Europe_WW1_Frontlines_as_of_1916.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Map_Europe_WW1_Frontlines_as_of_1916.png/330px-Map_Europe_WW1_Frontlines_as_of_1916.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Map_Europe_WW1_Frontlines_as_of_1916.png/440px-Map_Europe_WW1_Frontlines_as_of_1916.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Map_Europe_WW1_Frontlines_as_of_1916.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><b>Map Europe WW1 Frontlines as of 1916</b></div></div></div>\n<p>Two world wars and an economic depression dominated the first half of the 20th century. World War I was fought between 1914 and 1918. It started when <a href="/wiki/Archduke_Franz_Ferdinand_of_Austria" title="Archduke Franz Ferdinand of Austria">Archduke Franz Ferdinand of Austria</a> was assassinated by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Yugoslav_nationalism" title="Yugoslav nationalism">Yugoslav nationalist</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Gavrilo_Princip" title="Gavrilo Princip">Gavrilo Princip</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_407_149-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_407-149">[149]</a></sup> Most European nations were drawn into the war, which was fought between the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Entente_Powers" title="Entente Powers">Entente Powers</a> (<a href="/wiki/French_Third_Republic" title="French Third Republic">France</a>, <a href="/wiki/Belgium" title="Belgium">Belgium</a>, <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a>, Portugal, <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Russia</a>, the United Kingdom, and later <a href="/wiki/Italy" title="Italy">Italy</a>, <a href="/wiki/Greece" title="Greece">Greece</a>, <a href="/wiki/Romania" title="Romania">Romania</a>, and the United States) and the <a href="/wiki/Central_Powers" title="Central Powers">Central Powers</a> (<a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a>, <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bulgaria" title="Bulgaria">Bulgaria</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">Ottoman Empire</a>). The war left more than 16&#160;million civilians and military dead.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_440_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_440-150">[150]</a></sup> Over 60&#160;million European soldiers were mobilised from 1914 to 1918.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Serbian_retreat_WWI.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="415" data-file-width="577" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Serbian_retreat_WWI.jpg/220px-Serbian_retreat_WWI.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Serbian_retreat_WWI.jpg/330px-Serbian_retreat_WWI.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fb/Serbian_retreat_WWI.jpg/440px-Serbian_retreat_WWI.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Serbian_retreat_WWI.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Serbian_Campaign_of_World_War_I" title="Serbian Campaign of World War I">Serbian war efforts</a> (1914&#8211;1918) cost the country one quarter of its population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-153"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>Russia was plunged into the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Revolution" title="Russian Revolution">Russian Revolution</a>, which threw down the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Empire" title="Russian Empire">Tsarist monarchy</a> and replaced it with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Communist" title="Communist">communist</a> <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">Soviet Union</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_480_157-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_480-157">[157]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Austria-Hungary" title="Austria-Hungary">Austria-Hungary</a> and the Ottoman Empire collapsed and broke up into separate nations, and many other nations had their borders redrawn. The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Versailles" title="Treaty of Versailles">Treaty of Versailles</a>, which officially ended World War I in 1919, was harsh towards Germany, upon whom it placed full responsibility for the war and imposed heavy sanctions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_443_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_443-158">[158]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Excess deaths in Russia over the course of World War I and the <a href="/wiki/Russian_Civil_War" title="Russian Civil War">Russian Civil War</a> (including the postwar <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Russian_famine_of_1921" title="Russian famine of 1921">famine</a>) amounted to a combined total of 18 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-159"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup> In 1932&#8211;1933, under <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Stalin" title="Stalin">Stalin</a>\'s leadership, confiscations of grain by the Soviet authorities contributed to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Soviet_famine_of_1932-1933" title="Soviet famine of 1932-1933">second Soviet famine</a> which caused millions of deaths;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> surviving <a href="/wiki/Kulak" title="Kulak">kulaks</a> were persecuted and many sent to <a href="/wiki/Gulag" title="Gulag">Gulags</a> to do <a href="/wiki/Unfree_labour" title="Unfree labour">forced labour</a>. Stalin was also responsible for the <a href="/wiki/Great_Purge" title="Great Purge">Great Purge</a> of 1937&#8211;38 in which the <a href="/wiki/NKVD" title="NKVD">NKVD</a> executed 681,692 people;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> millions of people were <a href="/wiki/Population_transfer_in_the_Soviet_Union" title="Population transfer in the Soviet Union">deported and exiled</a> to remote areas of the Soviet Union.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Social_revolution" title="Social revolution">social revolutions</a> sweeping through Russia also affected other European nations following <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Great_War" title="The Great War">The Great War</a>: in 1919, with the <a href="/wiki/Weimar_Republic" title="Weimar Republic">Weimar Republic</a> in Germany, and the <a href="/wiki/First_Austrian_Republic" title="First Austrian Republic">First Austrian Republic</a>; in 1922, with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mussolini" title="Mussolini">Mussolini</a>\'s one party <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascist</a> government in the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Italy" title="Kingdom of Italy">Kingdom of Italy</a>, and in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ataturk" title="Ataturk">Ataturk</a>\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turkish_Republic" title="Turkish Republic">Turkish Republic</a>, adopting the Western alphabet, and state <a href="/wiki/Secularism" title="Secularism">secularism</a>.\nEconomic instability, caused in part by debts incurred in the First World War and \'loans\' to Germany played havoc in Europe in the late 1920s and 1930s. This and the <a href="/wiki/Wall_Street_Crash_of_1929" title="Wall Street Crash of 1929">Wall Street Crash of 1929</a> brought about the worldwide <a href="/wiki/Great_Depression" title="Great Depression">Great Depression</a>. Helped by the economic crisis, social instability and the threat of communism, <a href="/wiki/Fascism" title="Fascism">fascist movements</a> developed throughout Europe placing <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a> in power of what became <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">Nazi Germany</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hobsbawn_163-0"><a href="#cite_note-hobsbawn-163">[163]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_438_164-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_438-164">[164]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1933, Hitler became the leader of Germany and began to work towards his goal of building Greater Germany. Germany re-expanded and took back the <a href="/wiki/Saarland" title="Saarland">Saarland</a> and <a href="/wiki/Rhineland" title="Rhineland">Rhineland</a> in 1935 and 1936. In 1938, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> became a part of Germany following the <a href="/wiki/Anschluss" title="Anschluss">Anschluss</a>. Later that year, following the <a href="/wiki/Munich_Agreement" title="Munich Agreement">Munich Agreement</a> signed by Germany, France, the United Kingdom and Italy, Germany annexed the <a href="/wiki/Sudetenland" title="Sudetenland">Sudetenland</a>, which was a part of <a href="/wiki/Czechoslovakia" title="Czechoslovakia">Czechoslovakia</a> inhabited by ethnic Germans, and in early 1939, the remainder of Czechoslovakia was split into the <a href="/wiki/Protectorate_of_Bohemia_and_Moravia" title="Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia">Protectorate of Bohemia and Moravia</a>, controlled by Germany, and the <a href="/wiki/Slovak_Republic_(1939%E2%80%931945)" title="Slovak Republic (1939&#8211;1945)">Slovak Republic</a>. At the time, Britain and France preferred a policy of <a href="/wiki/Appeasement" title="Appeasement">appeasement</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Air_Force_Bomber_Command,_1942-1945._CL3400.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1772" data-file-width="2143" decoding="async" height="182" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Royal_Air_Force_Bomber_Command%2C_1942-1945._CL3400.jpg/220px-Royal_Air_Force_Bomber_Command%2C_1942-1945._CL3400.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Royal_Air_Force_Bomber_Command%2C_1942-1945._CL3400.jpg/330px-Royal_Air_Force_Bomber_Command%2C_1942-1945._CL3400.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/Royal_Air_Force_Bomber_Command%2C_1942-1945._CL3400.jpg/440px-Royal_Air_Force_Bomber_Command%2C_1942-1945._CL3400.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Royal_Air_Force_Bomber_Command,_1942-1945._CL3400.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Bombed and burned-out buildings in <a href="/wiki/Hamburg" title="Hamburg">Hamburg</a>, 1944/45</div></div></div>\n<p>With tensions mounting between Germany and <a href="/wiki/Second_Polish_Republic" title="Second Polish Republic">Poland</a> over the future of <a href="/wiki/Gda%C5%84sk" title="Gda&#324;sk">Danzig</a>, the Germans turned to the Soviets, and signed the <a href="/wiki/Molotov%E2%80%93Ribbentrop_Pact" title="Molotov&#8211;Ribbentrop Pact">Molotov&#8211;Ribbentrop Pact</a>, which allowed the Soviets to invade the Baltic states and parts of Poland and Romania. Germany <a href="/wiki/Invasion_of_Poland" title="Invasion of Poland">invaded Poland</a> on 1 September 1939, prompting France and the United Kingdom to declare war on Germany on 3 September, opening the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Theatre_of_World_War_II" title="European Theatre of World War II">European Theatre of World War II</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_465_165-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_465-165">[165]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Poland" title="Soviet invasion of Poland">Soviet invasion of Poland</a> started on 17 September and Poland fell soon thereafter. On 24 September, the Soviet Union attacked the <a href="/wiki/Soviet_occupation_of_the_Baltic_states_(1940)" title="Soviet occupation of the Baltic states (1940)">Baltic countries</a> and later, Finland. The British hoped to land at <a href="/wiki/Battles_of_Narvik" title="Battles of Narvik">Narvik</a> and send troops to aid Finland, but their primary objective in the landing was to encircle Germany and cut the Germans off from Scandinavian resources. Around the same time, Germany moved troops into Denmark. The <a href="/wiki/Phoney_War" title="Phoney War">Phoney War</a> continued.\n</p><p>In May 1940, Germany <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_France" title="Battle of France">attacked France</a> through the Low Countries. France capitulated in June 1940. By August Germany began a <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Britain" title="Battle of Britain">bombing offensive on Britain</a>, but failed to convince the Britons to give up.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_510_167-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_510-167">[167]</a></sup> In 1941, Germany invaded the Soviet Union in <a href="/wiki/Operation_Barbarossa" title="Operation Barbarossa">Operation Barbarossa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_532_168-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_532-168">[168]</a></sup> On 7 December 1941 <a href="/wiki/Empire_of_Japan" title="Empire of Japan">Japan</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Pearl_Harbor" title="Attack on Pearl Harbor">attack on Pearl Harbor</a> drew the United States into the conflict as allies of the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">allied</a> forces.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_511_169-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_511-169">[169]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_519_170-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_519-170">[170]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Yalta_Conference_(Churchill,_Roosevelt,_Stalin)_(B%26W).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2239" data-file-width="2720" decoding="async" height="181" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg/220px-Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg/330px-Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg/440px-Yalta_Conference_%28Churchill%2C_Roosevelt%2C_Stalin%29_%28B%26W%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Yalta_Conference_(Churchill,_Roosevelt,_Stalin)_(B%26W).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The "<a href="/wiki/Allies_of_World_War_II" title="Allies of World War II">Big Three</a>" at the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a> in 1945; seated (from the left): <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Franklin_D._Roosevelt" title="Franklin D. Roosevelt">Franklin D. Roosevelt</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Stalin" title="Joseph Stalin">Joseph Stalin</a></div></div></div>\n<p>After the staggering <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Stalingrad" title="Battle of Stalingrad">Battle of Stalingrad</a> in 1943, the German offensive in the Soviet Union turned into a continual fallback. The <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Kursk" title="Battle of Kursk">Battle of Kursk</a>, which involved the largest <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Prokhorovka" title="Battle of Prokhorovka">tank battle</a> in history, was the last major German offensive on the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Front_(World_War_II)" title="Eastern Front (World War II)">Eastern Front</a>. In June 1944, British and American forces invaded France in the <a href="/wiki/Normandy_landings" title="Normandy landings">D-Day landings</a>, opening a new front against Germany. Berlin finally <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Berlin" title="Battle of Berlin">fell in 1945</a>, ending World War II in Europe. The war was the largest and most destructive in human history, with <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_casualties" title="World War II casualties">60&#160;million dead across the world</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_439_171-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_439-171">[171]</a></sup> More than 40&#160;million people in Europe had died as a result of World War II,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup> including between 11 and 17&#160;million people who perished during <a href="/wiki/The_Holocaust" title="The Holocaust">the Holocaust</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup> The Soviet Union <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_casualties_of_the_Soviet_Union" title="World War II casualties of the Soviet Union">lost around 27&#160;million people</a> (mostly civilians) during the war, about half of all World War II casualties.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup> By the end of World War II, Europe had more than 40&#160;million <a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">refugees</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup> Several <a href="/wiki/World_War_II_evacuation_and_expulsion" title="World War II evacuation and expulsion">post-war expulsions</a> in Central and Eastern Europe displaced a total of about 20&#160;million people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup>\n</p><p>World War I and especially World War II diminished the eminence of Western Europe in world affairs. After World War II the map of Europe was redrawn at the <a href="/wiki/Yalta_Conference" title="Yalta Conference">Yalta Conference</a> and divided into two blocs, the Western countries and the communist Eastern bloc, separated by what was later called by <a href="/wiki/Winston_Churchill" title="Winston Churchill">Winston Churchill</a> an "<a href="/wiki/Iron_Curtain" title="Iron Curtain">Iron Curtain</a>". The United States and Western Europe\nestablished the <a href="/wiki/NATO" title="NATO">NATO</a> alliance and later the Soviet Union and Central Europe established the <a href="/wiki/Warsaw_Pact" title="Warsaw Pact">Warsaw Pact</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_530_177-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_530-177">[177]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schuman_Declaration.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="270" data-file-width="369" decoding="async" height="161" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e9/Schuman_Declaration.jpg/220px-Schuman_Declaration.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/e/e9/Schuman_Declaration.jpg/330px-Schuman_Declaration.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/e/e9/Schuman_Declaration.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Schuman_Declaration.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The <a href="/wiki/Schuman_Declaration" title="Schuman Declaration">Schuman Declaration</a> led to the creation of the <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a>. It began the <a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">integration process</a> of the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a> (<a href="/wiki/Europe_Day" title="Europe Day">9 May</a> 1950, at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/French_Foreign_Ministry" title="French Foreign Ministry">French Foreign Ministry</a>).</div></div></div>\n<p>The two new <a href="/wiki/Superpower" title="Superpower">superpowers</a>, the United States and the Soviet Union, became locked in a fifty-year-long Cold War, centred on <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_proliferation" title="Nuclear proliferation">nuclear proliferation</a>. At the same time <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Decolonisation" title="Decolonisation">decolonisation</a>, which had already started after World War I, gradually resulted in the independence of most of the European colonies in Asia and Africa.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_534_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_534-11">[11]</a></sup> In the 1980s the <a href="/wiki/Glasnost" title="Glasnost">reforms</a> of <a href="/wiki/Mikhail_Gorbachev" title="Mikhail Gorbachev">Mikhail Gorbachev</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Solidarity_(Polish_trade_union)" title="Solidarity (Polish trade union)">Solidarity</a> movement in Poland accelerated the collapse of the Eastern bloc and the end of the Cold War. Germany was reunited, after the symbolic <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall#Fall_of_the_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">fall of the Berlin Wall</a> in 1989, and the maps of Central and Eastern Europe were redrawn once more.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hobsbawn_163-1"><a href="#cite_note-hobsbawn-163">[163]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Europe.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="540" data-file-width="810" decoding="async" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/220px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/330px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/Flag_of_Europe.svg/440px-Flag_of_Europe.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_Europe.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Flag_of_Europe" title="Flag of Europe">Flag of Europe</a>, adopted by the <a href="/wiki/Council_of_Europe" title="Council of Europe">Council of Europe</a> in 1955 as the flag for the whole of Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p><a href="/wiki/European_integration" title="European integration">European integration</a> also grew after World War II. The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Rome" title="Treaty of Rome">Treaty of Rome</a> in 1957 established the <a href="/wiki/European_Economic_Community" title="European Economic Community">European Economic Community</a> between six Western European states with the goal of a unified economic policy and common market.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_536_179-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_536-179">[179]</a></sup> In 1967 the EEC, <a href="/wiki/European_Coal_and_Steel_Community" title="European Coal and Steel Community">European Coal and Steel Community</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Euratom" title="Euratom">Euratom</a> formed the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/European_Community" title="European Community">European Community</a>, which in 1993 became the <a href="/wiki/European_Union" title="European Union">European Union</a>. The EU established a <a href="/wiki/European_Parliament" title="European Parliament">parliament</a>, <a href="/wiki/European_Court_of_Justice" title="European Court of Justice">court</a> and <a href="/wiki/European_Central_Bank" title="European Central Bank">central bank</a> and introduced the <a href="/wiki/Euro" title="Euro">euro</a> as a unified currency.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_537_180-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_537-180">[180]</a></sup> Between 2004 and 2013, more Central and Eastern European countries began joining, <a href="/wiki/Enlargement_of_the_European_Union" title="Enlargement of the European Union">expanding the EU</a> to its current size of 28 European countries, and once more making Europe a major economical and political centre of power.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-natgeo_535_181-0"><a href="#cite_note-natgeo_535-181">[181]</a></sup> However, in June 2016 the people of the United Kingdom, in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_European_Union_membership_referendum,_2016" title="United Kingdom European Union membership referendum, 2016">non-binding referendum</a> on EU membership voted to <a href="/wiki/Brexit" title="Brexit">leave the European Union</a>.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Europe" title="Geography of Europe">Geography of Europe</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Europe_topography_map_en.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1198" data-file-width="1473" decoding="async" height="179" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Europe_topography_map_en.png/220px-Europe_topography_map_en.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Europe_topography_map_en.png/330px-Europe_topography_map_en.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Europe_topography_map_en.png/440px-Europe_topography_map_en.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Europe_topography_map_en.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Relief map of Europe and surrounding regions</div></div></div>\n<p>Europe makes up the western fifth of the <a href="/wiki/Eurasia" title="Eurasia">Eurasian</a> landmass.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encarta_21-1"><a href="#cite_note-Encarta-21">[21]</a></sup> It has a higher ratio of coast to landmass than any other continent or subcontinent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-182"><a href="#cite_note-182">[182]</a></sup> Its maritime borders consist of the Arctic Ocean to the north, the Atlantic Ocean to the west, and the Mediterranean, Black, and Caspian Seas to the south.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183">[183]</a></sup>\nLand relief in Europe shows great variation within relatively small areas. The southern regions are more mountainous, while moving north the terrain descends from the high <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathians</a>, through hilly uplands, into broad, low northern plains, which are vast in the east. This extended lowland is known as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Great_European_Plain" title="Great European Plain">Great European Plain</a>, and at its heart lies the <a href="/wiki/North_German_Plain" title="North German Plain">North German Plain</a>. An arc of uplands also exists along the north-western seaboard, which begins in the western parts of the islands of Britain and Ireland, and then continues along the mountainous, fjord-cut spine of Norway.\n</p><p>This description is simplified. Sub-regions such as the <a href="/wiki/Iberian_Peninsula" title="Iberian Peninsula">Iberian Peninsula</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Italian_Peninsula" title="Italian Peninsula">Italian Peninsula</a> contain their own complex features, as does mainland Central Europe itself, where the relief contains many plateaus, river valleys and basins that complicate the general trend. Sub-regions like <a href="/wiki/Iceland" title="Iceland">Iceland</a>, Britain, and Ireland are special cases. The former is a land unto itself in the northern ocean which is counted as part of Europe, while the latter are upland areas that were once joined to the mainland until rising sea levels cut them off.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Europe" title="Climate of Europe">Climate of Europe</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_Europe_present.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="850" data-file-width="1816" decoding="async" height="103" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Koppen-Geiger_Map_Europe_present.svg/220px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_Europe_present.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Koppen-Geiger_Map_Europe_present.svg/330px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_Europe_present.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Koppen-Geiger_Map_Europe_present.svg/440px-Koppen-Geiger_Map_Europe_present.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Koppen-Geiger_Map_Europe_present.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="K&#246;ppen climate classification">K&#246;ppen-Geiger climate classification</a> map for Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184">[184]</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:210px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Vegetation_Europe.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="158" data-file-width="208" decoding="async" height="158" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c5/Vegetation_Europe.png" width="208"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Vegetation_Europe.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Biome" title="Biome">Biomes</a> of Europe and surrounding regions: <br/> <span style="margin:0px; font-size:90%;"><span style="border:none; background-color:#9fd6c9; color:#9fd6c9;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Tundra" title="Tundra">tundra</a></span> <span style="margin:0px; font-size:90%;"><span style="border:none; background-color:#a7bddb; color:#a7bddb;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Alpine_tundra" title="Alpine tundra">alpine tundra</a></span> <span style="margin:0px; font-size:90%;"><span style="border:none; background-color:#006d64; color:#006d64;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Taiga" title="Taiga">taiga</a></span> <span style="margin:0px; font-size:90%;"><span style="border:none; background-color:#3c9798; color:#3c9798;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montane_forest" title="Montane forest">montane forest</a></span> <br/> <span style="margin:0px; font-size:90%;"><span style="border:none; background-color:#a4e05d; color:#a4e05d;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperate_broadleaf_forest" title="Temperate broadleaf forest">temperate broadleaf forest</a></span> <span style="margin:0px; font-size:90%;"><span style="border:none; background-color:#907699; color:#907699;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mediterranean_forest" title="Mediterranean forest">mediterranean forest</a></span> <span style="margin:0px; font-size:90%;"><span style="border:none; background-color:#f7ec6f; color:#f7ec6f;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperate_steppe" title="Temperate steppe">temperate steppe</a></span> <span style="margin:0px; font-size:90%;"><span style="border:none; background-color:#9b8447; color:#9b8447;">&#160;&#160;&#160;&#160;</span>&#160;<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Dry_steppe" title="Dry steppe">dry steppe</a></span></div></div></div>\n<p>Europe lies mainly in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Temperate" title="Temperate">temperate</a> climate zones, being subjected to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prevailing_westerlies" title="Prevailing westerlies">prevailing westerlies</a>. The climate is milder in comparison to other areas of the same latitude around the globe due to the influence of the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_Stream" title="Gulf Stream">Gulf Stream</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-climate_185-0"><a href="#cite_note-climate-185">[185]</a></sup> The Gulf Stream is nicknamed "Europe\'s central heating", because it makes Europe\'s climate warmer and wetter than it would otherwise be. The Gulf Stream not only carries warm water to Europe\'s coast but also warms up the prevailing westerly winds that blow across the continent from the Atlantic Ocean.\n</p><p>Therefore, the average temperature throughout the year of Naples is 16&#160;&#176;C (61&#160;&#176;F), while it is only 12&#160;&#176;C (54&#160;&#176;F) in New York City which is almost on the same latitude. Berlin, Germany; Calgary, Canada; and Irkutsk, in the Asian part of Russia, lie on around the same latitude; January temperatures in Berlin average around 8&#160;&#176;C (14&#160;&#176;F) higher than those in Calgary, and they are almost 22&#160;&#176;C (40&#160;&#176;F) higher than average temperatures in Irkutsk.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-climate_185-1"><a href="#cite_note-climate-185">[185]</a></sup> Similarly, northern parts of Scotland have a temperate marine climate. The yearly average temperature in city of Inverness is 9.05&#160;&#176;C (48.29&#160;&#176;F). However, Churchill, Manitoba, Canada, is on roughly the same latitude and has an average temperature of &#8722;6.5&#160;&#176;C (20.3&#160;&#176;F), giving it a nearly subarctic climate.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Geology">Geology</span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Geology_of_Europe" title="Geology of Europe">Geology of Europe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Geological_history_of_Europe" title="Geological history of Europe">Geological history of Europe</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mount_Elbrus_May_2008.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2000" data-file-width="3008" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Mount_Elbrus_May_2008.jpg/220px-Mount_Elbrus_May_2008.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Mount_Elbrus_May_2008.jpg/330px-Mount_Elbrus_May_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Mount_Elbrus_May_2008.jpg/440px-Mount_Elbrus_May_2008.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mount_Elbrus_May_2008.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Mount_Elbrus" title="Mount Elbrus">Mount Elbrus</a> in <a href="/wiki/Russia" title="Russia">Russia</a> is the highest mountain in Europe.</div></div></div>\n<p>The geological history of Europe traces back to the formation of the <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Shield" title="Baltic Shield">Baltic Shield</a> (Fennoscandia) and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sarmatian_craton" title="Sarmatian craton">Sarmatian craton</a>, both around 2.25&#160;billion years ago, followed by the <a href="/wiki/Volgo%E2%80%93Uralia" title="Volgo&#8211;Uralia">Volgo&#8211;Uralia</a> shield, the three together leading to the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/East_European_craton" title="East European craton">East European craton</a> (&#8776; <a href="/wiki/Baltica" title="Baltica">Baltica</a>) which became a part of the <a href="/wiki/Supercontinent" title="Supercontinent">supercontinent</a> <a href="/wiki/Columbia_(supercontinent)" title="Columbia (supercontinent)">Columbia</a>. Around 1.1&#160;billion years ago, Baltica and Arctica (as part of the <a href="/wiki/Laurentia" title="Laurentia">Laurentia</a> block) became joined to <a href="/wiki/Rodinia" title="Rodinia">Rodinia</a>, later resplitting around 550&#160;million years ago to reform as Baltica. Around 440&#160;million years ago <a href="/wiki/Euramerica" title="Euramerica">Euramerica</a> was formed from Baltica and Laurentia; a further joining with <a href="/wiki/Gondwana" title="Gondwana">Gondwana</a> then leading to the formation of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pangea" title="Pangea">Pangea</a>. Around 190&#160;million years ago, Gondwana and <a href="/wiki/Laurasia" title="Laurasia">Laurasia</a> split apart due to the widening of the Atlantic Ocean. Finally, and very soon afterwards, Laurasia itself split up again, into Laurentia (North America) and the Eurasian continent. The land connection between the two persisted for a considerable time, via <a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>, leading to interchange of animal species. From around 50&#160;million years ago, rising and falling sea levels have determined the actual shape of Europe, and its connections with continents such as Asia. Europe\'s present shape dates to the late <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tertiary_period" title="Tertiary period">Tertiary period</a> about five million years ago.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Encyclop&#230;dia_Britannica_186-0"><a href="#cite_note-Encyclop&#230;dia_Britannica-186">[186]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar-Europa-Point-LH-from-the-sea.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2112" data-file-width="2816" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Gibraltar-Europa-Point-LH-from-the-sea.jpg/220px-Gibraltar-Europa-Point-LH-from-the-sea.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Gibraltar-Europa-Point-LH-from-the-sea.jpg/330px-Gibraltar-Europa-Point-LH-from-the-sea.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b8/Gibraltar-Europa-Point-LH-from-the-sea.jpg/440px-Gibraltar-Europa-Point-LH-from-the-sea.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Gibraltar-Europa-Point-LH-from-the-sea.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Europa Point as seen from the <a href="/wiki/Strait_of_Gibraltar" title="Strait of Gibraltar">Strait of Gibraltar</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>The geology of Europe is hugely varied and complex, and gives rise to the wide variety of landscapes found across the continent, from the <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Highlands" title="Scottish Highlands">Scottish Highlands</a> to the rolling <a href="/wiki/Plain" title="Plain">plains</a> of Hungary.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187">[187]</a></sup> Europe\'s most significant feature is the dichotomy between highland and mountainous <a href="/wiki/Southern_Europe" title="Southern Europe">Southern Europe</a> and a vast, partially underwater, northern plain ranging from Ireland in the west to the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a> in the east. These two halves are separated by the mountain chains of the <a href="/wiki/Pyrenees" title="Pyrenees">Pyrenees</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alps" title="Alps">Alps</a>/<a href="/wiki/Carpathian_Mountains" title="Carpathian Mountains">Carpathians</a>. The northern plains are delimited in the west by the <a href="/wiki/Scandinavian_Mountains" title="Scandinavian Mountains">Scandinavian Mountains</a> and the mountainous parts of the British Isles.
