href="/wiki/Portal:Geography" title="Portal:Geography">Geography portal</a></span></li></ul></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notes">Notes</span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: lower-alpha;">\n</div>\n<div style=""><ol class="references" style="list-style-type:upper-alpha;">\n<li id="cnote_a"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <i><b><sup><a href="#ref_a_1">a</a> <a href="#ref_a_2">b</a></sup></b></i></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Transnistria" title="Transnistria">Transnistria</a>, internationally recognised as being a legal part of the <a href="/wiki/Moldova" title="Moldova">Republic of Moldova</a>, although <i>de facto</i> control is exercised by its internationally unrecognised government which declared independence from Moldova in 1990.</span></li>\n<li id="cnote_b"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_b_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Russia is considered a transcontinental country in both Eastern Europe and Northern Asia. The vast majority of its population (78%) lives in European Russia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Vishnevsky_251-0"><a href="#cite_note-Vishnevsky-251">[251]</a></sup> However only the population figure includes the entire state.</span></li>\n<li id="cnote_c"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <i><b><sup><a href="#ref_c_1">a</a> <a href="#ref_c_2">b</a> <a href="#ref_c_3">c</a></sup></b></i></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Guernsey" title="Guernsey">Guernsey</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Isle_of_Man" title="Isle of Man">Isle of Man</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jersey" title="Jersey">Jersey</a> are <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crown_Dependencies" title="Crown Dependencies">Crown Dependencies</a> of the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">United Kingdom</a>. Other <a href="/wiki/Channel_Islands" title="Channel Islands">Channel Islands</a> legislated by the <a href="/wiki/Bailiwick_of_Guernsey" title="Bailiwick of Guernsey">Bailiwick of Guernsey</a> include <a href="/wiki/Alderney" title="Alderney">Alderney</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sark" title="Sark">Sark</a>.</span></li>\n<li id="cnote_d"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <i><b><sup><a href="#ref_d_1">a</a> <a href="#ref_d_2">b</a></sup></b></i></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> can be considered part of Europe or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Southwest_Asia" title="Southwest Asia">Southwest Asia</a>; it has strong historical and sociopolitical connections with Europe. The population and area figures refer to the entire state, including the <i>de facto</i> independent part <a href="/wiki/Northern_Cyprus" title="Northern Cyprus">Northern Cyprus</a> which is not recognised as a sovereign nation by the vast majority of sovereign nations, nor the UN.</span></li>\n<li id="cnote_e"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_e_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Figures for <a href="/wiki/Portugal" title="Portugal">Portugal</a> include the <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">Azores</a> and <a href="/wiki/Madeira" title="Madeira">Madeira</a> archipelagos, both in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Northern_Atlantic" title="Northern Atlantic">Northern Atlantic</a>.</span></li>\n<li id="cnote_f"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_f_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Area figure for <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> includes <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>, a province that unilaterally declared its independence from <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> on 17 February 2008, and whose sovereign status is unclear. Population and density figures are from the first results of 2011 census and are given without the disputed territory of <a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a>.</span></li>\n<li id="cnote_g"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_g_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text">Figures for <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> include only <a href="/wiki/Metropolitan_France" title="Metropolitan France">metropolitan France</a>: some <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_France" title="Administrative divisions of France">politically integral parts of France</a> are geographically located outside Europe.</span></li>\n<li id="cnote_h"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_h_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> population for November 2014. Population and area details include European portion only: Netherlands and three entities outside Europe (<a href="/wiki/Aruba" title="Aruba">Aruba</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Cura&#231;ao">Cura&#231;ao</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a>) constitute the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_the_Netherlands" title="Kingdom of the Netherlands">Kingdom of the Netherlands</a>. <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a> is the official capital, while <a href="/wiki/The_Hague" title="The Hague">The Hague</a> is the administrative seat.</span></li>\n<li id="cnote_i"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_i_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> is physiographically considered a transcontinental country, mostly in Central Asia (UN region), partly in Eastern Europe, with European territory west of the <a href="/wiki/Ural_Mountains" title="Ural Mountains">Ural Mountains</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ural_River" title="Ural River">Ural River</a>. However, only the population figure refers to the entire country.</span></li>\n<li id="cnote_j"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_j_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> can be considered part of Eastern Europe or <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>; it has strong historical and sociopolitical connections with Europe. The population and area figures include the entire state respectively.</span></li>\n<li id="cnote_k"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_k_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> can be considered part of Europe or <a href="/wiki/Western_Asia" title="Western Asia">Western Asia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-252"><a href="#cite_note-252">[252]</a></sup> However the population and area figures are for the entire state. This includes the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exclave" title="Exclave">exclave</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Nakhchivan_Autonomous_Republic" title="Nakhchivan Autonomous Republic">Nakhchivan Autonomous Republic</a> and the region <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Nagorno-Karabakh">Nagorno-Karabakh</a> that has declared, and <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_unrecognised_countries" title="List of unrecognised countries">achieved</a>, independence. Nevertheless, it is not recognised <i><a href="/wiki/De_jure" title="De jure">de jure</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign states</a>.</span></li>\n<li id="cnote_l"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_l_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"> <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> can be considered part of Eastern Europe or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Asia" title="West Asia">West Asia</a>; it has strong historical and sociopolitical connections with Europe.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-253"><a href="#cite_note-253">[253]</a></sup> The population and area figures include Georgian estimates for <a href="/wiki/Abkhazia" title="Abkhazia">Abkhazia</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetia" title="South Ossetia">South Ossetia</a>, two regions that have declared and <i><a href="/wiki/De_facto" title="De facto">de facto</a></i> <a href="/wiki/List_of_states_with_limited_recognition" title="List of states with limited recognition">achieved</a> independence. <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Abkhazia_and_South_Ossetia#Positions_taken_by_states" title="International recognition of Abkhazia and South Ossetia">International recognition</a>, however, is limited.</span></li>\n<li id="cnote_m"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_m_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Turkey" title="Turkey">Turkey</a> is physiographically considered a transcontinental country, mostly in Western Asia (the Middle East) and Southeast Europe. Turkey has a small part of its territory (3%) in Southeast Europe called Turkish Thrace.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-254"><a href="#cite_note-254">[254]</a></sup> However only the population figure includes the entire state.</span></li>\n<li id="cnote_n"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <i><b><sup><a href="#ref_n_1">a</a> <a href="#ref_n_2">b</a> <a href="#ref_n_3">c</a> <a href="#ref_n_4">d</a></sup></b></i></span> <span class="reference-text">The total figures for area and population include only European portions of transcontinental countries. The precision of these figures is compromised by the ambiguous geographical extent of Europe and the lack of references for European portions of transcontinental countries.</span></li>\n<li id="cnote_o"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_o_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Kosovo" title="Kosovo">Kosovo</a> unilaterally declared its independence from <a href="/wiki/Serbia" title="Serbia">Serbia</a> on 17 February 2008. Its sovereign status is <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/International_reaction_to_the_2008_Kosovo_declaration_of_independence" title="International reaction to the 2008 Kosovo declaration of independence">unclear</a>. Its population is July 2009 CIA estimate.</span></li>\n<li id="cnote_p"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <i><b><sup><a href="#ref_p_1">a</a> <a href="#ref_p_2">b</a></sup></b></i></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Abkhazia" title="Abkhazia">Abkhazia</a> and <a href="/wiki/South_Ossetia" title="South Ossetia">South Ossetia</a>, both of which can be considered part of Eastern Europe or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Asia" title="West Asia">West Asia</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-W.Asia_255-0"><a href="#cite_note-W.Asia-255">[255]</a></sup> unilaterally declared their independence from <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> on 25 August 1990 and 28 November 1991 respectively. Their status as sovereign nations is <a href="/wiki/International_recognition_of_Abkhazia_and_South_Ossetia" title="International recognition of Abkhazia and South Ossetia">not recognised</a> by a vast majority of sovereign nations, nor the UN. Population figures stated as of 2003 census and 2000 estimates respectively.</span></li>\n<li id="cnote_q"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_q_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Nagorno-Karabakh">Nagorno-Karabakh</a>, which can be considered part of Eastern Europe or <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/West_Asia" title="West Asia">West Asia</a>, unilaterally declared its independence from <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a> on 6 January 1992. Its status as a sovereign nation is <a href="/wiki/Nagorno-Karabakh" title="Nagorno-Karabakh">not recognised</a> by any sovereign nation, nor the UN. Population figures stated as of 2003 census and 2000 estimates respectively.</span></li>\n<li id="cnote_r"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#ref_r_1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a href="/wiki/Greenland" title="Greenland">Greenland</a>, an autonomous constituent country within the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Danish_Realm" title="Danish Realm">Danish Realm</a>, is geographically a part of the continent of North America, but has been politically and culturally associated with Europe.</span></li>\n</ol></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span></h2>\n<div class="reflist" style="list-style-type: decimal;">\n<div class="mw-references-wrap mw-references-columns"><ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-UN_WPP-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-UN_WPP_1-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-UN_WPP_1-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-UN_WPP_1-2"><sup><i><b>c</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a class="external text" href="https://esa.un.org/unpd/wpp/DataQuery/" rel="nofollow">"World Population Prospects: The 2017 Revision"</a>. <i>ESA.UN.org</i> (custom data acquired via website). <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Department_of_Economic_and_Social_Affairs" title="United Nations Department of Economic and Social Affairs">United Nations Department of Economic and Social Affairs</a>, Population Division<span class="reference-accessdate">. Whether countries are considered in Europe or Asia can vary in sources, for example in the classification of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" title="CIA World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a> or that of the <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>. Note also that certain countries in Europe, such as France, have <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_countries_spanning_more_than_one_continent#Non-contiguous" title="List of countries spanning more than one continent">territories lying geographically outside Europe</a>, but which are nevertheless considered integral parts of that country.</span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Encarta-21"><span class="mw-cite-backlink">^ <a href="#cite_ref-Encarta_21-0"><sup><i><b>a</b></i></sup></a> <a href="#cite_ref-Encarta_21-1"><sup><i><b>b</b></i></sup></a></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation encyclopaedia">Microsoft Encarta Online Encyclopaedia 2007. <a class="external text" href="https://www.webcitation.org/5kwbxqnne?url=http://encarta.msn.com/encyclopedia_761570768/Europe.html" rel="nofollow"><i>Europe</i></a>. Both interactions proved costly and ultimately fatal.</q></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.btitle=The+Essential+World+History&amp;rft.pages=330&amp;rft.pub=Cengage+Learning&amp;rft.date=2010&amp;rft.isbn=978-0-495-90227-0&amp;rft.au=William+J.+Duiker&amp;rft.au=Jackson+J.+Spielvogel&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DUJpI18JaEL0C%26pg%3DPA330&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3AEurope"></span><link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r879151008" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/></span>\n</li>\n<li id="cite_note-Findlay2006-82"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-Findlay2006_82-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation book">Ronald Findlay (2006). <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=VOE-sRivB6kC&amp;pg=PA179" rel="nofollow"><i>Eli Heckscher, International Trade, And Economic History</i></a>. style="font-size:85%;"><div>\n<ul><li><sup>1</sup> Russia is a <a href="/wiki/List_of_transcontinental_countries" title="List of transcontinental countries">transcontinental country</a> in Eastern Europe and Northern Asia. The vast majority of its population (80%) lives in <a href="/wiki/European_Russia" title="European Russia">European Russia</a>, therefore Russia as a whole is included as a European country here.</li>\n<li><sup>2</sup> Turkey is a transcontinental country in the Middle East and Southeast Europe. It has a small part of its territory (3%) in Southeast Europe called <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Turkish_Thrace" title="Turkish Thrace">Turkish Thrace</a>.</li>\n<li><sup>3</sup> <a href="/wiki/Azerbaijan" title="Azerbaijan">Azerbaijan</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(country)" title="Georgia (country)">Georgia</a> are transcontinental countries. Both have a small part of their territories in the European part of the <a href="/wiki/Caucasus" title="Caucasus">Caucasus</a>.</li>\n<li><sup>4</sup> <a href="/wiki/Kazakhstan" title="Kazakhstan">Kazakhstan</a> is a transcontinental country. It has a small part of its territories located west of the Urals in Eastern Europe.</li>\n<li><sup>5</sup> <a href="/wiki/Cyprus" title="Cyprus">Cyprus</a> and <a href="/wiki/Armenia" title="Armenia">Armenia</a> are entirely in Southwest Asia, but has socio-political and historical connections with Europe.</li></ul>\n</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div></div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<p class="mw-empty-elt">\n</p>\n<div
